1457831656780</Time>
<rating>5<//rating>< review>
My son has been attending Sunshine House for 3 months now. He started 1 month after he turned 2 years old in December 2015. As a fellow educator, currently teaching 2nd grade and previously taught preschool, I was very specific in what I was looking for. I began looking into preschools in May 2015. Many people recommended Sunshine House for their academic program as well as emotional commitment to the children. I choose Sunshine House because I was drawn to their mixed age school and curriculum as well as cleanliness. I found the mixed age school very important because I want my son to have the option to work with kids his age as well as those older with more advance skills. Children learn best through watching, playing, and teaching other children. I was very pleased that Sunshine House allows children the opportunity to choose where they want to play during the free play while also providing structured educational activities. Sunshine House exposes him to various things from letters to critical thinking activities. Since enrolling I have already noticed an increase in his academics as well as language. I also appreciate that Sunshine House uses ASL and music as well as other mediums to teach subjects. I found them to be one of the most developmentally appropriate programs for the preschool age (2-5). I also found them to be the cleanliest facility. The staff is very thorough in cleaning rooms as well as toys. I anticipated that my son would get sick within the first few weeks, however after 3 months he has not been sick once. I also liked that they kept low teacher to student ratios and promoted healthy eating habits by providing healthy snacks and encouraging parents to pack healthy lunches. All of these reasons lead to my decision to enroll my son with them, but what is my number one reason now is their attention to my son. He had a great first 2 days then he started to have a difficult time transitioning. Every day the teachers took great care in comforting him when he was dropped off (either by me or my mother in law) and always gave updates during pick up. Since the children are able to play in different areas throughout the day they come into contact with various teachers and I have always been impressed with how informed each teacher has been about my son's day. When I came to pick up I always made an effort to watch my son before going to get him and I have seen how they comfort him when he's upset. Prior to enrollment I was very impressed with their program and philosophy but now I am more pleased with how they have helped my son adjust to preschool. He always says he loves preschool and now has transitioned beautifully. I highly recommend Sunshine House to any parent looking for a well-rounded, developmentally appropriate preschool. Their staff and program is exceptional!< /review>

< review>
Hey Nathan Brown, the church you went to is not affiliated with ours at all. We are in Santa Ana. There's a lot of churches called Newsong/New Song.

This Newsong is my home. Newsong accepts the fact that none of us are perfect while still creating an environment that gives everyone an opportunity to experience God's love and joy. <Review>Great pews, great news, great food, Papa Johns! Err I mean Newsong Church!

I started coming to Newsong 6-7 months ago and it feels like a study abroad program from all the different cultures and backgrounds melted into one campus. Coming from white megachurch all my life I have never experienced such a congregation that is here. 60% or so of the congregation at the campus is Asian which is a culture shock even from one Asian brother to another. I honestly had an adjustment period in the beginning of coming here that opened my eyes to what it truly looks like to do life with a multicultural, multigenerational diversely socioeconomic group of people that stretched me in a good way.

There are some pretty sweet fringe benefits from being a part of such a diverse group of people. Exhibit A: the post Sunday service lunch. Newsong has a crew of professional chefs in the congregation that donate their time and money to make huge soul food type of meals that make 4th Street Market look like a copycat. As a foodie I have to plug this, I mean if you don't enjoy pho, carne asada tacos with cilantro rice, or authentic bimbimbop with the poached egg on top you may be at the wrong church. Oh and not to mention there is an elote/shaved ice cart lady that they let also be a part of the action too. 5/5 stars for community lunches!

I could write an op-ed about all the rad community initiatives that Newsong does in Santa Ana for the homeless community, the youth and the immediate community surrounding the church. They intentionally moved their church from megachurch capital of the world in Irvine area to the Samaria of the OC and it wasn't a popular decision from what I've heard. I like that. That type of risk taking in the name of love for the poor and outcasts is what really keeps me coming back.< /Review><rating>5< /rating><user_id>106601526988621773220<//user_id></record>
</dataset><record>

< review>
This place is a must try . If you are ever in the area of Maricopa stop into Tina's Diner. We are working in Bakersfield and took the 45 minute drive to enjoy a taste of Heaven in the best meal I've had in a long time.  Tina takes pride in the food she puts out. If you leave her restaurant hungry you will never fill up. A bowl of soup ,then a salad plate(tossed salad,carrot salad, potato salad, and macaroni salad) then came a chicken fried steak with mashed potatoes and a cup of peaches. Can't forget the garlic bread.
The price was very affordable.  6 of us not one dissatisfied person.  Every thing made homemade and with love. My hat off to the great taste of Heaven.  When ever I'm near Tina you won my buisness.</review>

<userid>103355510243417190762<//userid><Name>Rudy Namikis<//Name>< Time>
1569218694644</Time>
< Rate>
5<//Rate>
< review>
Tina's is literally overflowing with character. Not only is the building thoroughly decorated, but Tina herself is an amazingly charismatic woman with tremendous stories of her life. Make sure to ask about how she survived as the 11th kid in a poor family in the Philippines!

The food is homemade and very delicious, with filling portions.

Depending on the season, Tina might just offer you a fresh, hand-picked guava. Take it!

Tina's is the full-spectrum antidote to the excess of chain restaurants and sanitized consumerism that plague our country. In many ways, I felt like I was back in 1910, grabbing a bite after a hard day in the oil fields and chatting with the owner.<//review>
